به الرابعة فقال اقتلوه فقالوا ياسول الله ! انما سرق قال اقطعوه فاتى به الخامسة فقال اقتلوه قال جابر فانطلقنا به فقتلناه (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب السارق يسرق مرارا ص ۲۵۷ نمبر ۴۴۱۰ رنسائی شریف، باب قطع اليدين والرجلين من السارق ص ۶۸۳ نمبر ۴۹۸۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تیسری اور چوتھی مرتبہ بھی ہاتھ اور پاؤں کاٹا جائے گا کیونکہ چوری کی ہے۔ سرق ثالثا لم يقطع وخلد في السجن حتى يتوب
The right hand of the thief is cut from the wrist and cauterized. [2553] (31) If he steals a second time, his left foot is cut. This hadith also indicates that the right hand is cut. And that the hand is cut from the joint. The proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet cut a thief's hand from the joint. This hadith indicates the hand is cut from the joint, and after cutting the wound is cauterized to prevent excessive blood loss and death, because cutting the hand severs the artery. However, if there is a new method other than cauterization to stop blood, it can be used. The hadith is: from Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Thawban that the Messenger of Allah said: Cut it and then cauterize it. So they cut and cauterized. This hadith indicates to cauterize after cutting. Zanad: wrist. Tahsim: will be cauterized. End [2553 (31) So if he steals a second time, his left foot is cut. If he steals a third time, it is not cut and he is imprisoned until he repents. If he steals a second time, the left foot is cut; then if he steals a third time, the left hand is not cut. Rather, such a thief is imprisoned until he repents from theft. If both hands or both feet are cut, how can he eat, drink, perform wudu, and relieve himself? He becomes disabled. So after the left foot is cut, he is imprisoned. Evidence for this is the athar: Ali was brought a thief who had stolen, so he cut his hand. Then he was brought again having stolen, so he cut his foot. Then he was brought a third time having stolen, so he ordered him to prison and said: Leave for him a foot to walk on and a hand to eat and clean himself with. This athar indicates that after cutting the left foot, nothing more is cut so he can perform wudu and istinja. Imam al-Shafi'i says: If he steals a third time, his left hand is cut; if he steals a fourth time, his right foot is cut. The hadith is like this: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that a thief was brought to the Prophet and he said: Kill him. They said: O Messenger of Allah, he only stole. He said: Cut him. He said: So he was cut. Then he was brought a second time, he said: Kill him. They said: He only stole. He said: Cut him. He said: So his foot was cut. Then he was brought a third time, he said: Kill him. They said: He only stole. He said: Cut his hand. Then he was brought a fourth time, he said: Kill him. They said: He only stole. He said: Cut his foot. Then he was brought a fifth time, he said: Kill him. Jabir said: So we went and killed him. This hadith indicates that the hand and foot are also cut on the third and fourth times because he stole. He who steals a third time is not cut and is imprisoned until he repents.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the extent of amputation for repeated theft. The Hanafi position, based on the athar of Ali, holds: first theft cuts the right hand from the wrist, second cuts the left foot, then for any further theft the thief is imprisoned indefinitely until repentance. The reason given is practical necessity: the thief needs one hand for eating, wudu, and istinja, and one foot for walking. Cutting more would render him entirely dependent. Imam al-Shafi'i, citing a hadith from Jabir, holds that the amputations continue alternately: third offense cuts the left hand, fourth cuts the right foot, and only on the fifth offense is execution permitted. The Hanafi response is implicit: the athar of Ali is preferred because it aligns with the principle of preserving the thief's basic functions. The passage also clarifies that the initial cut is from the wrist (not the elbow) and that cauterization is recommended, though modern medical alternatives are permissible. This disagreement has practical consequences: in the Hanafi school, a habitual thief faces only one hand and one foot amputation then imprisonment, whereas in the Shafi'i school up to four amputations are possible before execution.

Key Terms
زند (zand): The wrist joint; the point from which the hand is amputated.
تحسم (tahsim): Cauterization of the wound after amputation to prevent bleeding.
خلد في السجن (khullida fi al-sijn): Imprisoned indefinitely until repentance; not for a fixed term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a thief who steals a third time after already having his right hand and left foot amputated?
A) His left hand is amputated.
B) His right foot is amputated.
C) He is imprisoned until he repents.
D) He is executed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits amputation to one hand and one foot to preserve the thief's ability to perform basic necessities, then imposes indefinite imprisonment.

No Amputation When Left Hand is Paralyzed or Right Foot Missing
Ruling on exception to hand amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi exception to hadd amputation when the left hand is missing/paralyzed or the right foot is missing, and explain the rationale based on preserving basic functions.

Core Idea
If cutting would leave no hand for wudu/istinja or no limb for balance, the hand is not cut.

The hadd punishment for theft is amputation of the right hand, but the Hanafi school recognizes exceptional circumstances where this punishment is not applied. This lesson examines two specific cases: when the left hand is already paralyzed or missing, and when the right foot is already missing. The rationale is to avoid complete incapacitation and to preserve the basic human functions of purification and mobility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
Recall the general hadd for theft: amputation of the right hand. This lesson deals with exceptions.
2
Identify the first exception
If the left hand is paralyzed (ashall) or already amputated, the right hand is not cut. Why? To allow the thief to perform wudu and istinja with the right hand.
The left hand is the usual hand for cleaning, but if it is unavailable, the right hand must be preserved.
3
Identify the second exception
If the right foot is already missing, the right hand is not cut either. Why? Cutting both the right hand and foot (same side) would destroy balance and prevent walking.
The left foot is unaffected, but balance requires opposite limbs; losing both on one side makes walking extremely difficult.
4
State the alternative punishment
In both exceptions, the thief is imprisoned until he repents. This is not a lesser penalty but an adjustment to avoid excessive harm.
Imprisonment until repentance (tawba) is a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) in these cases.
5
Identify the legal basis
The ruling is based on an athar from Ali (رضي الله عنه) who said he would not leave a thief with no hand to eat and clean himself. This reflects the Hanafi principle that punishments are not meant to destroy human dignity or basic functions.
The athar is recorded in Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۵۵۴] (۳۲) وان كان السارق اشبل اليد اليسرى او اقطع او مقطوع الرجل اليمنى لم يقطع۔ اگر چور کا بائیں ہاتھ شل ہو یا کٹا ہوا ہو یا دائیں پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہو تو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ چور کا دائیں ہاتھ کا نا تھا لیکن پہلے ہی سے بائیں ہاتھ کٹا ہوا ہے یاشل ہے اس لئے اس ہاتھ سے وضو استنجاء نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے دائیں ہاتھ بھی کاٹ دیں تو دونوں ہاتھوں سے محروم ہو جائے گا۔ اور کسی ہاتھ سے وضو، استنجاء نہیں کر پائے گا۔ اس لئے اس کا دائیں ہاتھ بھی نہیں کاٹا جائے گا تا کہ دائیں ہاتھ سے وضو استنجا کر سکے۔ اور اگر پہلے سے دایاں پاؤں کٹا ہوا ہے پس اگر دائیں ہاتھ بھی کاٹ دیں تو بالکل نہیں چل پائے گا کیونکہ ایک ہی طرف کے ہاتھ پاؤں دونوں کٹ جائیں تو بیلنس خراب ہونے کی وجہ سے چلنانا ممکن ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اب دایاں ہاتھ بھی نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ البتہ تو بہ کرنے تک قید میں ڈال دیا جائے گا۔ اثر میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے۔ كان على لا يقطع الايد والرجل وان سرق بعد ذلك سجن ونكل وكان يقول اني لستحيى الله الا ادع له يدا ياكل بها ويستنجى (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قطع السارق ج عاشر ص ۱۸۶ نمبر ۱۸۷۶۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ میں کھانے اور استنجاء کے لئے بھی کوئی ہاتھ نہ چھوڑوں اس سے شرمندگی ہوتی ہے اس لئے بایاں ہاتھ شل ہو تو دایاں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اشل : شل ہوا ہاتھ، مرا ہوا ہا تھے۔
[2554] (32) If the thief's left hand is paralyzed or cut off, or his right foot is cut off, his hand is not cut. If the thief's left hand is already paralyzed or cut, he cannot perform wudu and istinja with that hand. So if we cut his right hand, he would be deprived of both hands and unable to perform wudu and istinja. Therefore his right hand is also not cut so he can perform wudu and istinja with his right hand. And if his right foot is already cut, then if we also cut his right hand, he will not be able to walk at all because if the hand and foot on the same side are cut, balance is lost and walking becomes impossible. Therefore his right hand is also not cut. Rather, he is imprisoned until he repents. There is an indication of this in the athar: Ali would only cut the hand and foot, and if he stole after that, he would imprison and punish him. He used to say: I am ashamed before Allah to not leave him a hand to eat and clean himself. This athar indicates that if the left hand is paralyzed, the right hand is not cut. Ashall: paralyzed hand, dead hand.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying exceptions to the hadd amputation for theft. The Hanafi school holds that if the left hand is already missing or paralyzed, the right hand is not cut because the thief would then have no hand for wudu and istinja, causing unbearable hardship. Similarly, if the right foot is already missing, the right hand is not cut to preserve the ability to walk (balance requires opposite limbs). In such cases, the thief is imprisoned until repentance instead. The ruling is based on the athar of Ali where he explicitly said he would not leave a thief with no hand to eat and clean himself, showing mercy and preserving basic human functions. The rationale is that the hadd penalty is not meant to cause complete incapacity; the goal is deterrence and justice, not destruction.

Key Terms
اشل (ashall): Paralyzed or withered hand, often one that cannot be used for grasping or cleaning.
استنجاء (istinja): Cleaning after relieving oneself, required for ritual purity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi alternative punishment when a thief's left hand is paralyzed so the right hand is not cut?
A) The thief is fined double the stolen amount.
B) The thief is imprisoned until he repents.
C) The thief is given lashes instead.
D) The thief is released with a warning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes basic human needs (wudu, istinja, walking) over the literal application of fixed punishments when the punishment would lead to total incapacitation.

Two Conditions for Amputation in Theft
Ruling stating two procedural conditions for hadd amputation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required before a thief's hand is amputated according to Hanafi law and explain why each condition is necessary.

Core Idea
Amputation for theft requires both the stolen property's presence and the victim's demand — without either, the hadd is not applied.

This lesson introduces two procedural conditions that must be fulfilled before the hadd punishment for theft can be carried out. Understanding these conditions clarifies that hudud penalties are not automatic but have strict safeguards against doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The stolen property itself (or its value) must be physically present at the time of execution. This ensures that the theft is proven beyond doubt.
If the property is lost or consumed, doubt arises and hadd is suspended.
2
Identify the second condition
The victim (owner) must demand the cutting of the hand. This is because the hadd is a right of Allah that becomes established through the victim's claim.
The victim may forgive, which prevents the punishment.
3
Understand the rationale
These conditions prevent punishment in cases of doubt (shubha). The Hanafi school emphasizes shubha in hudud to avoid errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۵۵۵] (۳۳) ولا يُقطع السارق مگر یہ کہ جس کا چرایا ہے وہ حاضر ہو اور چوری کرنے کا دعوی کرے۔ ہاتھ کاٹنے کے لئے دو شرطیں ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ مسروق منہ ہاتھ کاٹنے کا مطالبہ کرے اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ہاتھ کاٹنے کے وقت مسروق حاضر ہو۔
[2555] (33) The thief's hand is not cut unless that which was stolen is present and he claims the theft. There are two conditions for cutting the hand: first, the victim demands the cutting of the hand; second, at the time of cutting, the stolen property is present.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying two necessary conditions before the hadd amputation for theft can be implemented. First, the victim (owner of the stolen property) must demand the cut. This is because the hadd is a right of Allah, but it is initiated based on the victim's claim; the victim may also forgive. Second, the stolen property itself must be present (or its value equivalent) at the time of execution. These conditions ensure that the theft is proven and that the penalty is not applied in cases of doubt or absence of evidence. The Hanafi school emphasizes procedural safeguards in hudud punishments. The conditions are derived from the general principles of Islamic criminal law.

Key Terms
مسروق منہ (masruq minhu): The person from whom the property was stolen (the victim or owner).
مسروق (masruq): The stolen property itself; must be present at the time of amputation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two conditions must be met before a thief's hand is amputated according to this passage?
A) The thief confesses and the stolen goods are worth over 10 dirhams.
B) The stolen property is present and the victim demands the cut.
C) Two witnesses testify and the thief is an adult.
D) The theft occurred at night and the thief is a repeat offender.

Key Takeaway
Amputation for theft is not automatic; it requires both the stolen property's presence and the victim's demand.

Theft Hadd: When Nisab Condition Fails After Theft
Explains ruling and proof for non-cut when nisab no longer met

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school drops the hadd of hand cutting when the stolen item's value drops below nisab, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the athar of Ayman and the hadith of Safwan.

Core Idea
The hadd of theft requires nisab at the time of cutting — if value drops, no cut.

The Hanafi school holds that the hadd penalty for theft is contingent on the stolen item meeting the nisab threshold at the moment of punishment. This lesson examines a scenario where the thief sells the item back to the owner or its value decreases below nisab after the theft but before the hadd is carried out. We will explore the proof from the athar of Ayman and contrast it with the Shafi'i position based on the hadith of Safwan.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling from the matn: if the thief sells the stolen item to the owner or its value drops below nisab, the hand is not cut.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Find the dalil: the athar from Ayman that the hand was only cut in the Prophet's time for a shield worth one dinar. This shows nisab at cutting is necessary.
Qawl Sahabi (saying of a Companion) is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Identify the opposing position and proof
State the Shafi'i opinion and the riwaya from Abu Yusuf: after the qadi's judgment, the hadd is not dropped. Their proof is the hadith of Safwan where the Prophet said, 'Could you not have done this before bringing him to me?'
The hadith implies that after judgment the hadd is established.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school responds: the hadith of Safwan applies before the hadd becomes due, not after. The athar of Ayman directly ties the cut to the item's value, making nisab a condition at the time of cutting.
Hanafis prioritize the explicit practice over the general implication of Safwan's hadith.
5
Determine the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: if the thief sells the item or value drops before the qadi's ruling, Hanafis do not cut; Shafi'is and Abu Yusuf's riwaya would cut if the judge has already ruled.
The key is the timing of the value drop relative to the qadi's judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باعها منه او نقصت قيمتها عن النصاب لم يقطع اور نصاب سے قیمت کم ہو جائے تو نہیں کاٹا جائے گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ایمن قال لم تقطع اليد في زمان رسول الله الا في مجن وقيمته يومئذ دينار (الف) ( سن لیستی ، باب اختلاف الناقلين في ثمن الجن ج عامن ص ۸ نمبر ۴ ۱۷ ۷ ار ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما قطع فیه السارق ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۴۳۸۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نصاب سے قیمت کم ہو جائے تو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اور ایک روایت امام ابو یوسف کی بھی ہے کہ فیصلے کے بعد چور سے بیچ دے یا هبہ کر دے یا قیمت کم ہو جائے تو پھر بھی حد لگے گی۔ کیونکہ قاضی کا فیصلہ ہو چکا ہے (۲) حدیث صفوان میں حضور کے فیصلے کے بعد بیچنے کی خواہش ظاہر کی یا معاف کرنے کی خواہش ظاہر کی تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ میرے پاس آنے سے پہلے اور فیصلے سے پہلے یہ سب کرنا چاہئے تب حد ساقط ہوتی فیصلے کے بعد ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ حدیث کا ٹکڑا یہ ہے۔ قال فاتيته فقلت اتقطعه من اجل ثلاثين درهما؟ انا ابيعه وانسئه ثمنها قال فهلا كان هذا قبل ان تاتيني به (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فیمن سرق من حرزص ۲۵۵ نمبر ۴۳۹۴ رنسائی شریف ما یکون حرز او مالا یکون ص ۶۷۳ نمبر ۷ ۴۸۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے میرے پاس لانے سے پہلے کیوں ایسا نہ کر لیا تو معاف ہو جاتا۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ فیصلہ کرنے کے بعد تو کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا ۔ فقطعه رسول الله الله ( نسائی شریف نمبر ۴۸۸۲)
He sold it from him or its value decreased from the nisab: he is not cut. And if the value becomes less than the nisab, then it will not be cut. Its proof is this athar: from Ayman who said: 'The hand was not cut in the time of the Messenger of Allah except for a shield, and its value on that day was a dinar.' From this athar it is known that if the value becomes less than the nisab, the hand will not be cut. Imam al-Shafi'i says, and there is also a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, that after the judgment if the thief sells it or gives it as a gift or its value decreases, still the hadd will be applied because the qadi's judgment has been passed. (2) In the hadith of Safwan, after the Prophet's judgment, he expressed a desire to sell or forgive, so the Prophet said: 'You should have done this before bringing him to me.' So the hadd would be dropped before judgment, not after. The portion of the hadith is: He said: 'I came to him and said, will you cut his hand for thirty dirhams? I will sell it and defer its price?' He said: 'Could you not have done this before bringing him to me?' In this hadith it is that before bringing him to me, why did you not do so? So he would have been forgiven. Meaning that after the judgment, it will be cut. And in another hadith, 'So he cut his hand' - only the Messenger of Allah cut it.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the effect of a change in the stolen item's value or possession after the theft but before the hadd. The author first presents the matn: if the thief sells the stolen item back to the owner or its value drops below nisab, the hand is not cut. The commentary explains the proof: the athar from Ayman ibn Umm Ayman that in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) the hand was only cut for a shield worth one dinar. This shows that nisab is a condition at the time of cutting. Then the author mentions the view of Imam al-Shafi'i and a riwaya from Imam Abu Yusuf: they hold that after the qadi's judgment, the hadd is not dropped even if the thief sells or the value drops, citing the hadith of Safwan where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Should you not have done this before bringing him to me?' The Hanafi response is not explicitly stated but the proof of the athar is preferred, and the hadith of Safwan is interpreted as applying before the hadd is established, not after. The author then provides the text of the hadith and a second hadith: 'So he cut his hand' from Nasa'i. The Hanafi ruling remains that the hadd is not applied if the nisab condition is not met at the time of cutting.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum value threshold for the hadd of theft to apply, which is ten dirhams or one dinar.
قيمتها (qimatuhā): The market value of the stolen item at the time of the theft or cutting.
مجن (mijann): A shield, used as the example of the stolen item in the athar of Ayman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a thief steals an item worth ten dirhams, but before the hand is cut, its value drops to five dirhams?
A) The hand is cut because the theft was of a nisab value.
B) The hand is not cut because the nisab condition is not met at the time of cutting.
C) The hand is cut regardless of the value drop.
D) The hand is cut only if the thief sells the item.

Key Takeaway
The hadd of hand cutting is not applied if the stolen item's value falls below nisab before the punishment is carried out.

Ruling on Re-stealing the Same Item After Hand Cut
States a specific exception in the law of theft (sariqah).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the hand is not cut again for re-stealing the same item and explain the legal reasoning (the thief's share).

Core Idea
A thief who loses his hand for a stolen item gains a share in it, so re-stealing the same item does not warrant another cut.

Islamic criminal law (hudud) prescribes severe penalties for theft, but with careful exceptions. One such exception arises when the thief re-steals the exact same item after having already been punished for it. The Hanafi school rules that the hand is not cut a second time, because the first cut transferred a share of ownership to the thief. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the underlying logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stealing the same item again after the hand has been cut for it and the item returned. The ruling is that the hand is not cut again.
Note the condition: the item must be in the same state (ʿayn). If transformed, the ruling may differ.
2
Locate the proof
The text cites an athar (tradition) from al-Shaʿbi: one who steals from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) is not cut because he has a share in it. This serves as the basis for analogy.
The athar is found in Musannaf ʿAbd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The effective cause (ʿilla) is that the thief has a share in the item. The hand cut gives the thief a share in the stolen article. Therefore, re-stealing it is like stealing one's own property in part.
The Hanafi school uniquely recognizes this share; other schools may not.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the stolen item is lost while with the thief after the cut, he is not liable for compensation, confirming the share concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۵) ومن سرق عينا فقطع فيها وردها ثم عاد فسرقها وهى بحالها لم يقطع کسی نے کوئی چیز چرائی پس اس میں ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور اس نے اس کو واپس کر دیا پھر دوبارہ اس کو چھالیا اور وہ چیز پہلی حالت پر ہے تو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ مثلا کسی نے برتن چرایا جس کی وجہ سے اس کا ہاتھ کا ٹا گیا۔ اس نے برتن مالک کو واپس دے دیا، بعد میں پھر اس برتن کو اسی چور نے چرا لیا اور برتن کے بدلے ایک مرتبہ ہاتھ کٹ چکا تو گویا کہ اس برتن میں کچھ حصہ چور کا بھی ہو گیا اور جس میں چور کا حصہ ہو اس کے چرانے میں ہاتھ نہیں کہتا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر چور کے پاس سے وہ برتن گم ہو جاتا تو اس پر برتن کا تاوان لازم نہیں ہوتا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشعبی قال لا يقطع من سرق من بيت المال لان له فيه نصيبا (ج) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل يسرق شیئالہ فیہ نصیب ج عاشرص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۸۸۷۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر چوری کے مال میں چور کا حصہ ہو تو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ ہاتھ کٹنے کی وجہ سے برتن میں چور کا حصہ ہو گیا ہے اس لئے دوبارہ ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔
(35) Whoever steals an item, and his hand is cut for it, and he returns it, then he steals it again while it is in the same state: he is not cut. For example, someone stole a pot, so his hand was cut for it. He returned the pot to the owner. Later, that same thief stole that same pot again. Since his hand was cut once in exchange for the pot, he has acquired a share in that pot. If there is a thief's share in something, his stealing it does not warrant cutting. This is why if that pot had been lost with the thief, he would not be liable for its compensation. (2) There is an athar from al-Sha'bi who said: 'One who steals from the treasury is not cut because he has a share in it.' This athar shows that if the thief has a share in the stolen property, the hand is not cut. Because of the cut, the thief gained a share in the pot, so the hand is not cut again.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author presents the matn: if someone steals an item, has his hand cut, returns the item, then steals it again while it remains in the same state, the hand is not cut again. The commentary explains the reasoning: because the thief, having lost his hand in exchange for the item, acquires a share in it. This is similar to the athar from al-Sha'bi that one who steals from bait al-mal is not cut because he has a share in it. Thus, the thief's share prevents the second cut.

Key Terms
عين (ʿayn): The specific stolen item in its original state, not transformed.
حصہ (hissah): A share or partial ownership acquired by the thief through the hand cut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the item is now less than nisab in value.
B) Because the thief has already been punished and cannot be punished twice for the same crime.
C) Because the thief has a share in the item from the first cut.
D) Because the owner has forgiven the thief.

Key Takeaway
The thief's acquisition of a share through the hand cut prevents the reapplication of the hadd penalty for stealing the same item in its original state.

Re-stealing a Transformed Item: The Hadd Applies Again
Ruling on re-stealing after transformation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on re-stealing a transformed item and explain why the hand is cut again, identifying the principle of legal identity change.

Core Idea
A transformed item is a new entity; the thief's previous cut does not grant a share in it.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses a unique scenario in hudud: when a thief steals an item, is punished, returns it, and then the item undergoes a fundamental transformation (e.g., thread into cloth). The text rules that a second theft of the transformed item triggers the hadd again. This ruling rests on a key Hanafi principle: when the substance and name of an item change, its legal identity is renewed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is stealing the transformed item (cloth). The ruling is that the hand is cut (hadd applied).
This is not a repetition of the first theft; it is a new theft of a legally different object.
2
Understand the transformation
The example: thread (ghazl) becomes cloth (thawb) through weaving. The transformation changes both the substance (asliyyat) and the name (ism).
Hanafis consider this a complete change in legal identity, unlike a mere change in ownership or location.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The text states the principle: 'if a thing's substance changes and its name changes, it is no longer the same thing in legal ruling; it becomes a separate entity.' This is a minor qa'idah (legal maxim).
This principle is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may treat the transformation differently (e.g., as a change in value rather than identity).
4
Apply the principle to the case
The first theft of thread gave the thief a 'share' (shubha) in the thread, which prevented the hadd from being applied again on the same item. But after transformation, the thief has no share in the cloth, so the hadd is reapplied.
The 'share' arises because the thief's hand was already cut for that item; Islamic law does not double-punish for the same property, but transformation removes that protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۶) وان تغيرت عن حالها مثل ان كانت غزلا فسرقه فقطع فيه ورده ثم نسج فعاد وسرقه قطع اور اگر وہ چیز اپنی حالت سے بدل گئی مثلا یہ کہ سوت چرایا تھا پس اس میں ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اس کو واپس کر دیا پھر کپڑا بن دیا پھر اس کو چرایا تو ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ پہلے جب چرایا تھا وہ چیز کچھ اورتھی اور دوبارہ اس چیز کو چرایا تو اس کی حالت اتنی بدل گئی تھی کہ کچھ اور نام ہوگیا۔ مثلا پہلے سوت چرایا تھا جس کی وجہ سے ہاتھ کاٹا گیا۔ چور نے سوت واپس کر دیا۔ مالک نے اس سوت سے کپڑا بن لیا اب اس کا نام سوت نہیں رہا بلکہ کپڑا ہو گیا۔ اب اس کو اسی چور نے چرایا تو دوبارہ ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اب پہلی چیز نہیں رہی جس میں اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا تھا اور ایک گونہ اس میں چور حصہ دار بن گیا تھا بلکہ یہ دوسری چیز بن گئی ہے اور اس میں چور کا حصہ نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کے چرانے میں چور کا ہاتھ دوبارہ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ چیز کی اصلیت بدل جائے اور نام بھی بدل جائے تو وہ چیز حکم کے اعتبار سے پہلی چیز نہیں رہتی وہ الگ شئی ہو جاتی ہے۔
(36) And if it has changed from its state, for example if it was thread and he stole it, and his hand was cut for it, and he returned it, then it was woven into cloth, and he stole it again: he is cut. And if the item has changed from its state, for example, he stole thread, so his hand was cut for it. He returned it, then the owner wove it into cloth. Then the same thief stole it. He will be cut again. The previous thing is no longer the same; the thief had gained a share in it, but this is a different thing, and the thief has no share in it. So for stealing it, the thief's hand will be cut again. The principle is: if a thing's substance changes and its name changes, it is no longer the same thing in legal ruling; it becomes a separate entity.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This ruling states that if the stolen item has changed from its original state (e.g., thread was woven into cloth), and the thief steals it again, the hand is cut. The reason is that the item has become a different entity; the thief's previous cut gave him a share in the original item, but not in the transformed one. The principle is that when the substance and name change, the legal identity changes.

Key Terms
تغيرت (taghayyarat): Changed state or form, such that the item's legal identity is altered.
غزلا (ghazlan): Thread or yarn, used as an example of a raw material that changes into cloth.
اصلیت (asliyyat): Original substance or essence of the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The hand is not cut because the cloth is still the same property.
D) The hand is cut only if the cloth is worth nisab.

Key Takeaway
Under Hanafi law, a stolen item that undergoes a change in substance and name becomes a new legal entity, so re-stealing it incurs the hadd again.

Liability of Thief After Hand Cut
States ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning the stolen item after the hand is cut, and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i on whether compensation is due if the item is destroyed.

Core Idea
The hand cut replaces financial liability; the stolen item is returned if extant, but no compensation if destroyed.

This passage addresses a specific situation in the law of theft (sariqa): after the hadd punishment of cutting the hand is carried out, what happens to the stolen property? The Hanafi school holds that the penalty of the cut itself compensates for the loss, so the thief is not liable for the value if the item is destroyed. However, if the stolen item still exists, it remains the owner's property and must be returned. This lesson explores the proofs from hadith and athar, and the difference with Imam al-Shafi'i who requires compensation even after the cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
From the matn: if the stolen item (ayn qa'imah) is still in the thief's possession after the hand cut, he must return it. If it is destroyed (halaka), he does not guarantee it (la yadman).
The ruling distinguishes between the item's existence and its destruction.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf: 'لا غرم على السارق بعد قطع يمينه' (No compensation on the thief after cutting his right hand). This is a zanni al-thubut hadith but clear in its dalala against liability.
The hadith is from al-Daraqutni; its chain is considered sound by many.
3
Examine the supporting athar
The athar of 'Ata' states that compensation is not required unless the stolen item is found extant, in which case it is taken from him. This reinforces the Hanafi position.
The athar emphasizes that the return of the extant item is a separate duty from compensation.
4
State the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the thief is liable for the value of the stolen item even after the cut, based on a mursal statement of al-Hasan al-Basri: 'هو ضامن للسرقة مع قطع يده'.
The opposing proof is weaker due to its mursal chain and contradiction with the explicit hadith.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If the stolen item is destroyed after the cut, Hanafis do not require payment; Shafi'is do. This affects the owner's right to compensation in such cases.
The difference arises from whether the hadd punishment replaces financial liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۷) واذا قطع السارق والعين قائمة في يده ردَّها وان كانت هالكة لم يضمن اگر چور کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور وہ چیز بعینہ اس کے ہاتھ میں موجود ہے تو اس کو واپس کرے گا اور اگر ہلاک ہو چکی ہے تو ضامن نہیں ہو گا چور نے مثلا برتن چرایا جس کی وجہ سے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا گیا اور برتن بعینہ موجود ہے تو چور پر لازم ہے کہ برتن مالک کی طرف واپس کرے۔ اور اگر برتن ضائع ہو چکا ہے تو چور پر اس کی قیمت ادا کر نالازم نہیں ہے۔ برتن کے بدلے ہاتھ کاٹا گیا تو مالک کو کچھ نہ کچھ بدلائل گیا ہے۔ اس لئے برتن کے بدلے قیمت لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ ہاں ! برتن موجود ہو تو چونکہ حقیقت میں یہ مالک کا ہے اس لئے اس پر واپس کرنالازم ہو گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا غرم على السارق بعد قطع يمينه (الف) (دار قطنی، کتاب الحدود والدیات ج ثالث ص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۳۳۶۳ سفن لیبتی ، باب عزم السارق ج ثامن ص ۴۸۱ نمبر ۱۷۲۸۳) اور چیز بعینہ موجود ہو تو مالک کی طرف واپس کرنا ہو گا اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن عطاء قال لا يغرم السارق بعد قطع يمينه الا ان توجد السرقة بعينها فتوخذ منه (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة في السارق تقطع يده يتبع بالسرقة ج خامس ص ۴۷۵ نمبر ۲۸۱۲۹ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب عزم السارق ج عاشر ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۷ ۱۸۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ تاوان تو لازم نہیں ہوگا البتہ وہ چیز موجود ہو تو مالک کی طرف واپس کروائی جائے گی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ہاتھ کٹنے کے بعد چور سے چیز ہلاک ہو جائے تو اس کا تاوان مالک کی طرف واپس کرنا ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل میاثر ہے۔ عن الحسن انه كان يقول هو ضامن للسرقة مع قطع يده ۔ ایک دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن
(37) And when the thief is cut and the item is still in his hand, he returns it; and if it is destroyed, he does not guarantee it. If the thief's hand is cut and the item is still in his possession, he will return it. And if it is destroyed, he will not be liable. For example, a thief stole a pot, so his hand was cut. If the pot is still there, the thief is required to return it to the owner. If the pot is lost, he is not required to pay its value. Because the hand was cut in exchange for the pot, the owner has received some compensation. So compensation for the pot is not required. Yes, if the pot exists, since it is actually the owner's, he must return it. (2) There is a hadith from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf who said: the Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, there is no compensation on the thief after cutting his right hand.' And if the item exists, it must be returned to the owner, and its proof is this athar from 'Ata' who said: 'The thief does not pay compensation after cutting his right hand unless the stolen item is found in his possession, then it is taken from him.' From this athar it is known that compensation is not obligatory, but if the item exists, it is returned to the owner. Imam al-Shafi'i says: after the hand is cut, if the item is destroyed with the thief, he must return its compensation to the owner. Their proof is a mursal from al-Hasan who used to say: 'He is liable for the theft along with the cutting of his hand.' Another narration from...
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the liability of the thief after the hand is cut. The matn rules: if the stolen item is still in the thief's possession after the cut, he must return it; if it is destroyed, he does not guarantee its value (no daman). The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Awf: 'There is no compensation on the thief after his right hand is cut.' And the athar of 'Ata: he is not liable except if the stolen item is found extant, then it is taken from him. Then the author mentions Imam al-Shafi'i's view: the thief is liable for the value if the item is destroyed, citing the statement of al-Hasan. The Hanafi position is that the penalty of hand cutting replaces the compensation; the thief's hand is taken in exchange for the stolen property, so he is not liable additionally. However, if the item is still extant, it is the owner's property and must be returned.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Liable for compensation or guarantee of the stolen property.
غرم (ghurm): Financial compensation or penalty paid for the stolen item.
عين قائمة (ayn qa'imah): The stolen item still in existence and identifiable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if after the thief's hand is cut, the stolen item is found to be in the thief's possession?
A) The thief must return the item to the owner.
B) The thief keeps the item as compensation for his hand.
C) The thief must pay the value of the item.
D) The item becomes the property of the state.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely holds that the hand cut replaces the financial liability for the stolen item, but does not extinguish the obligation to return the item if it still exists.

Effect of Thief's Claim of Ownership on Hadd
Ruling that thief's claim of ownership nullifies hadd even without evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a thief's claim of ownership and explain why the hadd is dropped based on the principle of shubha.

Core Idea
A thief's mere claim of ownership creates doubt, dropping the hadd even without evidence.

In Hanafi law, hudud punishments are suspended by doubts. This lesson examines a case where a thief, after stealing, claims the item belongs to him. Even without proof, the claim raises a shubha, and the hand is not amputated. We will explore the ruling, its rationale, and the evidence from the athar of Ata.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The thief claims ownership after theft. The ruling is that the hadd (amputation) is dropped, even if he provides no evidence.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites an athar from Ata: if a suspect claims to have bought or found the item, he is not cut nor punished.
The athar is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لم يقطع ولم يعاقب' indicates that the hadd is dropped based on the claim alone, without requiring proof of ownership.
This demonstrates that shubha overrides the hadd.
4
Note the underlying principle
The ruling is grounded in the maxim 'Hudud are suspended by doubts.' The claim creates a doubt about the thief's share in the property.
This principle is consistently applied in Hanafi fiqh.

واذا ادعى السارق ان العين المسروقة ملكه سقط القطع عنه وان لم يقم بينة [ہندی] اگر چور نے دعوی کیا کہ مسروقہ چیز اس کی ملکیت ہے تو اس سے کاٹنا ساقط ہو جائے گا اگر چہ اس پر بینہ قائم نہیں کئے۔ چور نے چوری کے بعد دعوی کر دیا کہ یہ چیز میری ملکیت ہے تو اس دعوی کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا، چاہے ملکیت کہنے کے بعد اس پر گواہ پیش نہ کر سکا ہو۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اوپر گزرا کہ چوری کے مال میں چور کا حصہ ہو جائے یا حصے کا شبہ ہو جائے تب بھی نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ یہاں ملکیت کے دعوی کے بعد حصے کا شبہ ہو گیا اس لئے حد ساقط ہو جائے گی (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ خریدنے کا صرف دعوی کیا تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ قال عطاء ان وجدت سرقة مع رجل سوء يتهم فقال ابتعتها فلم ينفذ ممن ابتاعها منه او قال وجدتها لم يقطع ولم يعاقب (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۵۱افی الرجل انهم يوجد معه المتاع ج خامس ص ۵۵۰ نمبر ۲۸۹۱۳ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التهمة ج عاشر ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۸۸۹۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خریدنے کا دعوی کرے پھر بھی حد ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ چاہے بینہ پیش نہ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس اثر میں خریدنے پر بینہ پیش نہیں کیا پھر بھی حد ساقط ہوگئی۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ شبہ ہو جائے تو حد ساقط ہو جائے گی، البتہ مال کا تاوان دینا پڑے گا۔ [حاشیہ] (الف) حضرت حسن سے مروی ہے کہ وہ فرماتے تھے کہ وہ ضامن ہوگا مسروقہ چیز کے لئے اس کے ہاتھ کے کاٹنے کے ساتھ ۔ حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا مسروقہ چیز کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اس کو خود ہلاک کیا ہو یا ہلاک نہ کیا ہو۔ اور چور کا ہاتھ کاٹنا بھی ہے (ب) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا اگر چوری کی چیز کسی متہم برے آدمی کے پاس پائیں۔ پس وہ کہے کہ میں نے اس کو خریدا ہے تو جس سے خریدا ہے اس سے بیچ نافذ نہیں ہوگی یا کہے کہ میں نے اس چیز کو پایا ہے تو نہ ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا اور نہ سزا دی جائے گی۔
And if the thief claims that the stolen item is his property, the cutting (of his hand) is dropped from him even if he does not provide evidence. [Urdu:] If the thief claims after theft that the item is his property, then the cutting is dropped even if he does not provide witnesses. The reason is that a doubt arises about his share. This is supported by the athar of Ata: 'If you find stolen goods with a suspicious man and he says “I bought it” but his purchase is not recognized from whom he bought it, or he says “I found it,” he is not cut nor punished.' And the margin notes add reports from Hasan and Ibrahim confirming that the thief is liable for the value but the hadd is dropped.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Theft. The author states that if a thief, after committing theft, claims that the stolen item actually belongs to him, the hadd punishment (amputation of the hand) is waived even if he does not bring witnesses to prove his claim. The reason given in the commentary is that this claim creates a doubt (shubha) that the thief might have a share in the property. The principle in Hanafi law is that hadd punishments are suspended by doubt. The passage then cites an athar from Ata that if a suspect claims he bought the item or found it, he is not cut or punished. This supports the ruling. The margin notes add reports from Hasan and Ibrahim confirming that the thief is liable for the value of the item even if the hadd is dropped.

Key Terms
القطع (al-qat'): Amputation of the hand as a hadd punishment for theft.
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt that suspends the application of hadd punishment.
ضمان (daman): Financial liability or guarantee; here, the obligation to pay the value of the stolen item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hand is not cut, but he must pay the value.

D) He is imprisoned until he proves ownership.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a thief's claim of ownership, even without proof, creates a doubt that suspends the hadd punishment, but financial liability remains.

Punishment for Highway Robbers Caught Before Theft or Murder
Ruling on punishment for highway robbers caught before theft or murder

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for highway robbers caught before theft or murder and identify the two proofs (Quran and athar) that support it.

Core Idea
A highway robber caught before taking property or killing is imprisoned until repentance — not amputated or executed.

This lesson examines the precise punishment for highway robbers when they are apprehended before actually committing theft or murder. The Hanafi school distinguishes this situation from the full hadd punishments mentioned in Surah al-Ma'idah. We will see how the imam applies a lesser punishment based on Quranic text and the practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is highway robbery (qat' al-tariq). The ruling applies only when the robber is caught before taking any property or killing anyone. The punishment is imprisonment until repentance.
The ruling does not apply if property or life is taken.
2
Locate the two proofs
The passage cites two proofs: the Quranic verse (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33) and an athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
The Quranic proof is qat'i al-thubut (definitive transmission), while the athar is zanni (probable).
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse lists four punishments: execution, crucifixion, cross-amputation, or exile. The Hanafi school interprets 'exile' (nafy) as imprisonment, and this option is chosen when no theft or murder occurred.
The other three punishments apply only after actual theft or murder.
4
Analyze the athar proof
Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote that a thief should not be cut until he takes the goods out of the house. This shows that the hadd of cutting requires actual removal of property. By analogy, a highway robber who has not taken property is not subject to amputation.
The athar reinforces the principle that completion of the crime is a condition for severe punishment.
5
State the practical application
The imam does not amputate or execute such robbers but imprisons them until their repentance is evident. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
Repentance is determined by outward signs (حركات وسكنات).

البيت بالمتاع ج خامس ص ۴۷۴ نمبر ۲۸۱۱۴ / مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب السارق يوجد فى البيت ولم يخرج ج عاشر ص ۱۹۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۰۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال چرا کر قبضہ کرے گا تب ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ اس And if a group of obstructors or one who is able to obstruct come out intending highway robbery, and they are seized before taking any property or killing any soul, the imam imprisons them until they show repentance. [Urdu:] If a group capable of highway robbery emerges, or a single person capable, and they are arrested before taking property or killing, the imam does not cut their hands or kill them but imprisons them until repentance is evident. This is supported by the athar of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz: 'He wrote concerning a thief that he should not be cut until he takes the goods out of the house, perhaps he repents before leaving.' And the Quranic verse (5:33) lists punishments including exile, which is interpreted as imprisonment when no theft or murder occurred.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage addresses the punishment for highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq) who are apprehended before they actually commit theft or murder. The author states that the imam does not amputate their hands or execute them, but imprisons them until they repent. The reasoning is that since no property has been taken and no life has been taken, the conditions for the full hadd (cutting of hands and feet or execution) are not met. The passage provides two proofs: an athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz showing that a thief is not cut until he removes the goods from the house, and the Quranic verse on the punishment of those who wage war against Allah and His messenger (al-ma'ida 5:33), which lists four punishments including exile (nafy), interpreted here as imprisonment. This applies when the robber has not yet taken property or killed.

Key Terms
قطع الطریق (qat' al-tariq): Highway robbery; literally 'cutting the road' i.e., blocking and robbing travelers.
ممتنع (mumtani'): Obstructor; one who prevents passage, i.e., a highway robber.
توبة (tawba): Repentance; the condition for release from imprisonment in this context.

Conditions for Cross-Amputation in Highway Robbery: The Nisab and Protected Property
Ruling on cross-amputation for highway robbers when each gets at least 10 dirhams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for applying the hadd of cross-amputation to highway robbers and identify which property qualifies as protected.

Core Idea
Cross-amputation applies only when each highway robber's share reaches ten dirhams from the loot of a protected person (Muslim or dhimmi).

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the punishment for highway robbers who actually take property. The text specifies that the hadd of cross-amputation is applied when each member's individual share meets the nisab of ten dirhams, and the victim's property is legally protected. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the hudud punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is highway robbery (hirabah) where property is taken. The ruling is cross-amputation (cutting right hand and left foot) by the imam.
This is a fixed hadd punishment.
2
List the conditions for the ruling
Two conditions: (1) The property taken must belong to a Muslim or dhimmi (protected). (2) Each robber's share of the loot must be at least ten dirhams (or equivalent value).
The nisab is per individual, not total.
3
Distinguish between protected and unprotected property
Property of a Muslim or dhimmi is protected (mahfuz). Property of a harbi (enemy combatant) is not protected, so no hand-cutting for taking it.
This is based on the concept of protected wealth.
4
Explain why the nisab is per individual
The text says 'when divided among them, each reaches ten dirhams.' This means each robber's personal share must meet the nisab; the total loot may be large but if shares are small, the hadd does not apply.
This prevents excessive punishment for minor involvement.
5
Apply to a scenario
Five robbers steal 30 dirhams from a Muslim. Each share is 6 dirhams, below nisab. No cross-amputation. If they steal 60 dirhams, each share 12 dirhams, then hadd applies.
Ensure each robber's share is calculated after division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اخذوا مال مسلم او ذمى والماخوذ اذا قسم على جماعتهم بلغ كل رجل منهم عشرة دراهم او اكثر او بلغهم ما قيمته ذلك قطع الامام ايديهم و ارجلهم من خلاف [ہندی] اس جماعت نے ذمی کا مال یا مسلمان کا مال لوٹا اور اتنا مال لوٹا کہ جماعت کے ہر فرد کو دس درہم یا دس درہم سے زیادہ ملے گا ۔ یا لوٹا ہوا مال ہر ایک آدمی کو اتنا اتنا ملے گا کہ اس کی قیمت دس درہم ہوگی تو امام ہر ایک کا دایاں ہاتھ اور بایاں پاؤں کاٹے گا۔ ذمی یا مسلمان کا مال لوٹنے سے اس لئے کا نا جائے گا کہ وہ مال محفوظ ہے۔ اور حربی کا مال لوٹا تو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا کیونکہ اس کا مال محفوظ نہیں ہے۔ اور ہر ایک کو دس درہم پہنچے تب کا ٹا جائے گا اس کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے کہ دس درہم سے کم میں نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور دایاں ہاتھ
And if they take property of a Muslim or a dhimmi, and the taken property, when divided among their group, reaches each man ten dirhams or more, or reaches them what is equivalent in value, then the imam cuts off their hands and feet from opposite sides. [Urdu:] If the group loots property of a dhimmi or Muslim and each receives ten dirhams or more, or property of that value, the imam cuts off each one's right hand and left foot. The cutting is because the property of a Muslim or dhimmi is protected. If they loot a harbi's property, the hand is not cut because their property is not protected. The condition of ten dirhams is based on the established nisab for theft, as previously explained.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage states the punishment for highway robbers who actually take property and each member's share reaches the nisab of ten dirhams. The imam applies cross-amputation: cutting the right hand and left foot. The condition is that the victim's property is protected (Muslim or dhimmi). The property of a harbi (enemy) is not protected, so no cutting. The nisab (ten dirhams) is the same as for ordinary theft, as the proof for that has already been established earlier. The commentary emphasizes that the cutting is only when each individual's share reaches the nisab, not the total loot.

Key Terms
قطع الايدي والارجل من خلاف (qat' al-aydi wa al-arjul min khilaf): Cross-amputation: cutting the right hand and left foot.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen under Islamic rule whose property is protected.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim from enemy territory whose property is not protected.

Hadd for Highway Robbery: Amputation of Right Hand and Left Foot
Explains the hadd for hiraba with Quranic and Sunnah evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a highway robber who takes property, identify the Quranic and Sunnah proofs, and explain why this differs from the punishment for ordinary theft.

Core Idea
Highway robbery triggers a distinct hadd: amputation of right hand and left foot.

In this passage, the author addresses a critical distinction in Islamic criminal law: the punishment for highway robbery (hiraba) versus simple theft (sariqa). While theft is punished by cutting the right hand, highway robbery—which threatens public security—warrants a harsher, cross-amputation. The ruling is grounded in the Quranic verse 5:33 and the prophetic practice in the hadith of the 'Ukl and 'Uraynah tribes. By studying this lesson, you will learn the precise ruling, its evidence, and the wisdom behind the severity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the case: highway robbers who take property (each gets 10 dirhams or more) but do not kill. The punishment is amputation of the right hand and left foot.
The value threshold (nisab) matches that of theft: 10 dirhams.
2
Identify the primary proof: Quran 5:33
Locate the verse: 'فقطعوا أيديهم وأرجلهم من خلاف' (Cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides). The imperative 'فقطعوا' indicates obligation, and 'من خلاف' specifies the cross-limb amputation.
The verse is general (amm) and requires interpretation (tawil) to derive the specific ruling.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the text prove the ruling? The command is unconditional for the crime of hiraba. The phrase 'من خلاف' (from opposite sides) means the right hand and left foot are cut, not the left hand and right foot.
The Hanafi school holds that the imperative indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarina (indication) otherwise.
4
Apply the Sunnah precedent
The hadith of 'Ukl and 'Uraynah shows the Prophet (ﷺ) cutting the hands and feet of those who stole camels after apostasy and murder. Even though murder was also involved, the amputation was for the theft, and the cross-amputation demonstrates the practice for hiraba.
The Hanafi school uses this hadith as a supporting evidence (muayyid) for the Quranic ruling.
5
Distinguish from ordinary theft
Simple theft (sariqa) requires cutting only the right hand (not from opposite sides) and does not involve the element of public fear. The hadd for hiraba is more severe because it threatens community safety.
The distinction is based on the illa (effective cause) of causing public fear and insecurity.

Source Text

Book of Theft. If each of them gets ten dirhams or more, or what is equivalent in value, the Imam cuts off their hands and feet from opposite sides. (Explanation:) Their left foot and right hand will be cut. The reason is that these are not mere thieves but highway robbers. Once highway robbery occurs, the entire area is fearful for months and insecurity spreads. Therefore, a severe punishment is prescribed: cut one side's hand and the other side's foot so that they cannot repeat the crime. (2) The punishment for taking property is mentioned in the verse: 'Cut off their hands and feet from opposite sides' (Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 33). This verse says that the hands and feet of robbers should be cut. (3) Hadith: Some people from the tribes of 'Ukl and 'Uraynah came to the Prophet (ﷺ), embraced Islam, and stayed in Madinah. They fell ill, so the Prophet told them to go to the camels of sadaqah and drink their milk and urine. They recovered but then apostatized, killed the camel herders, and drove away the camels. The Prophet sent people after them, and they were brought back. He cut off their hands and feet, and branded their eyes with hot irons until they died. The full hadith: Anas said: 'Some people from 'Ukl came to the Prophet (ﷺ)...' [Bukhari and Muslim]. This hadith shows that the hands and feet of highway robbers are cut because they stole the camels, and because they killed the herders, their eyes were branded so that they would die in agony. Footnote (a): Anas said: A group from the tribe of 'Ukl came to the Prophet (ﷺ). They accepted Islam, then their stomachs became swollen, so he ordered them to go to the camels of sadaqah and drink their milk and urine. They did so, recovered, then apostatized, killed the herders, and drove away the camels. The Prophet sent people after them; they were brought back. So he cut off their hands and feet and branded their eyes, and did not cauterize them until they died.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and Sunnah. It addresses the case of highway robbers (muharibun) who take property but do not commit murder. The prescribed punishment is amputation of the right hand and left foot, based on Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33. The author explains the wisdom behind the severity: highway robbery disrupts public security. The hadith of 'Ukl and 'Uraynah is cited as practical application: the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered amputation of hands and feet for stealing camels. Although the hadith also involves murder (they killed the herders), the amputation was for the theft. This illustrates that the hadd for theft (sariqa) is amputation of hand only, but for highway robbery (hiraba), it is amputation from opposite sides. The footnote clarifies the hadith details.

Key Terms
محارب (muharib): A highway robber who uses force to steal, causing public fear.
قطع (qat'): Amputation of the hand and foot as a hadd punishment.

Ruling for Highway Robbers Who Kill: Hadd Execution and No Pardon by Wali
Ruling with proof on hiraba resulting in murder without theft.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for highway robbers who kill but do not take property and explain why the victim's family cannot pardon.

Core Idea
Highway robbers who kill are executed as hadd; the victim's family cannot pardon because public security overrides private right.

This passage addresses a critical intersection of hudud and qisas: when highway robbers kill but do not steal, the punishment is execution as a hadd, not merely qisas. The author argues that the ruler must carry out the sentence regardless of the victim family's forgiveness, citing Quranic verses and an early precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiraba (highway robbery) resulting in murder without theft. The ruling is execution as a hadd punishment.
The author specifies that this is a hadd, not just qisas.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 5:33 (أو يقتلوا) and 5:45 (النفس بالنفس), plus an athar from al-Zuhri.
These proofs establish both the basis for execution and the ruler's authority.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'or they are killed' in 5:33 combined with the qisas principle in 5:45 makes execution mandatory. The athar confirms the ruler's exclusive authority.
The context of hiraba makes this a hadd, overriding the family's right to pardon.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may view it as pure qisas, but the Hanafi position classifies it as hadd due to the public threat.
The cross-madhhab difference affects whether the family can pardon.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that this is a hadd, which cannot be waived by the victim's family because the crime harms public order.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(41) And if they killed a person and did not take property, the Imam kills them as a hadd punishment. So if the heirs (of the victim) forgive them, even then the Imam does not accept their forgiveness. (Explanation: The robbers did not take property but killed someone, so the Imam will execute them as qisas. Even if the victim's heirs forgive, the Imam will not forgive but will execute them. The verse for life for life has passed: 'We prescribed for them therein that life for life, eye for eye' (Quran 5:45). This verse shows that if they killed, they will be killed in return. In the verse of hiraba, there is also 'or they are killed' (Quran 5:33). That is, highway robbers should be killed. And the forgiveness of the heirs does not drop qisas because their evil is very great. (3) Athar: from al-Zuhri: 'The punishment of the highway robber is up to the ruler; the forgiveness of the blood heir is not permissible; that is up to the Imam.' This athar shows that the matter is in the hands of the ruler; the heir is not allowed to forgive. Footnote (a): al-Zuhri said: The punishment of the highway robber is up to the ruler; the forgiveness of the blood heir is not permissible; it is up to the Imam.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the case where highway robbers kill but do not take property. The punishment is execution, and it is a hadd (fixed penalty) rather than mere qisas, meaning the victim's family cannot pardon. The author cites Quran 5:45 (life for life) and 5:33 (or they are killed) as evidence. Additionally, an athar from al-Zuhri clarifies that the ruler has authority over the punishment, not the blood heir. The key point is that the severity of highway robbery (hiraba) overrides the right of pardon, because such crimes threaten public order.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by divine law for specific crimes.
ولى الدم (wali al-dam): The legal heir of the murder victim who has the right to demand qisas or pardon.
حرابة (hiraba): Highway robbery or armed banditry that threatens public security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Highway robbers who kill are executed as a hadd punishment; the victim's family cannot pardon because the crime is against public order.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Imam's Discretion for Highway Robbers Who Kill and Steal
Explains imam's discretion to combine punishments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the imam's discretionary options for punishing highway robbers who both kill and take property, and explain the evidence from Quran, hadith, and athar.

Core Idea
Two crimes, two penalties; imam may combine or choose only the greater.

When highway robbers both kill and steal, they have committed two separate hadd crimes. The Hanafi school holds that the imam has full discretion to impose any or all of the punishments mentioned in Quran 5:33—amputation, execution, crucifixion—or combine them as he deems appropriate. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the scope of the imam's choice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
State that the passage deals with highway robbers (muharibun) who both kill and take property. The Hanafi ruling gives the imam choice among amputation, execution, crucifixion, or any combination.
2
Locate the primary dalil from Quran
Quran 5:33 lists punishments separated by 'or' (aw). The Hanafi interpretation holds that 'or' indicates choice, not fixed sequence, giving the imam discretion.
Quran 5:33: '...that they be killed or crucified or have their hands and feet cut off from opposite sides...'
3
Examine the Sunnah and athar evidence
The hadith of 'Ukl and 'Uraynah (Bukhari) shows the Prophet applied both amputation and burning (a form of execution). The athar of 'Ata (Abd al-Razzaq) explicitly states the imam may choose any one or combine.
The hadith: 'He cut off their hands and feet and branded their eyes until they died.' Athar: 'Any of these the Imam wishes, he may judge them.'
4
Understand the scope of discretion
The imam may give separate punishments for each crime (amputation for theft, then execution for murder) or skip the lesser and apply only the greater (execution or crucifixion).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school restricts the imam's discretion; punishments are fixed according to the case. The Hanafi view gives more flexibility based on the particle 'aw' in the verse.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have strong evidence.

And if they killed and took property, the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he cuts off their hands and feet from opposite sides, and kills them and crucifies them; if he wishes, he kills them; and if he wishes, he crucifies them. (Surah al-Ma'idah 33). From this verse it is understood that if they killed, then in return they will be killed. In the verse of hiraba, there is 'or they are killed' (5:33). That is, highway robbers should be killed. And even if the heir forgives, qisas does not drop because their evil is very great. (3) Since they took property and also killed, there are two crimes, so both punishments can be given: amputation for property and execution for the murder. If the Imam deems fit, he can skip amputation and give the greater punishment of execution, or even the greater crucifixion, which involves disembowelment and being left on a plank for three days. In the hadith of 'Uraynah, their hands and feet were cut and then they were branded until death. The hadith fragment: Anas: 'They were brought to him, so he cut off their hands and feet and branded them, and did not cauterize them until they died' (Bukhari). This hadith shows both amputation and killing. And the Imam has discretion to leave a lesser punishment and apply a greater one at once. Evidence from athar: 'Ata said: Any of these the Imam wishes, he may judge them: if he wishes, he kills them, or crucifies them, or cuts off their hands and feet from opposite sides; if the Imam wishes, he does one of them and leaves the rest.' This shows he can give separate punishments or combine. Footnotes: (b) Anas said: The people of 'Ukl were brought, so he cut off their hands and feet and branded their eyes, then did not cauterize them until they died. (c) 'Ata said: The Imam may judge the highway robber as he wishes: if he wishes, he kills them, or crucifies them, or cuts off their hands and feet from opposite sides; and if the Imam wishes, he does one of them and leaves the rest.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage discusses the third scenario of highway robbery: both murder and theft. The imam has discretion to impose any or all of the punishments mentioned in Quran 5:33: amputation, execution, or crucifixion. The author explains that two crimes have been committed, so both penalties can apply. However, the imam may choose only the greater punishment if he sees fit. The hadith of 'Ukl and 'Uraynah is cited as precedent where both amputation and burning (crucifixion equivalent) were applied. The athar of 'Ata confirms the imam's discretion to combine or select. The footnote clarifies the hadith and athar sources.

Key Terms
صلب (salb): Crucifixion; a punishment where the criminal is left on a cross to die.
خيار (khiyar): The imam's discretionary choice among prescribed punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what options does the Imam have when highway robbers both kill and steal?
A) Must amputate only
B) Must execute only
C) Must crucify only
D) May amputate, execute, crucify, or any combination

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the imam full discretion to combine or select among amputation, execution, and crucifixion for highway robbers who both kill and steal, based on the particle 'aw' in the Quran and supporting sunnah and athar.

Imam's Discretion in Punishing Muharib Who Kill and Take Property
States ruling and proof for Imam's options when muharib kill and take property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three punishment options for a muharib who kills and takes property, and explain why the guardians' forgiveness is not accepted.

Core Idea
The Imam has full discretion to punish the muharib; the crime is a public right, not a private one.

This passage addresses a critical point in Islamic criminal law: the punishment for highway robbers who murder and loot. It clarifies that the matter is a public right, so the victim's family cannot pardon the offender. The Imam is given three severe options to choose from, based on the Quranic verse of hirabah and the practice of early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the crime
The passage addresses muharibun (highway robbers) who both kill and take property. This is a specific category of hirabah.
2
Recognize the nature of the punishment
The punishment is a hadd (fixed public right), not a private qisas. Hence, the guardians' forgiveness is irrelevant.
Compare with ordinary murder where qisas can be forgiven.
3
List the Imam's three options
The Imam may choose: (1) amputation of right hand and left foot, then execution and crucifixion; (2) execution only; (3) crucifixion only. The word 'aw' in the verse indicates choice.
The options are distinct; the Imam selects based on circumstances.
4
Understand the Quranic proof
Surah al-Ma'idah 5:33 provides the punishments connected by 'aw' (or), indicating discretion. The verse is qat'i in transmission but zanni in meaning regarding the exact application.
The athar from al-Zuhri reinforces that the ruler decides, not the guardians.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the Imam (or judge) weighs the severity of the crime, deterrence, and public interest to choose the appropriate punishment.
Modern analogies: armed robbery with murder, terrorism.

From this athar it is understood that his matter is the responsibility of the ruler; the guardian is not permitted to forgive.

This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the punishment of highway robbers (muharibun) who both kill and take property. It establishes that the guardians' forgiveness is irrelevant; the punishment is a matter for the Imam (ruler). The Imam has three choices: (1) cut off hands and feet from opposite sides, then kill and crucify; (2) kill only; (3) crucify only. The proof is from the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah verses 5:33 and 5:45) and the athar of al-Zuhri. The reasoning is that the crime is so severe that it transcends private rights; it is a public order crime. The Imam's discretion is emphasized.

Key Terms
محارب (muharib): One who commits hirabah (highway robbery with arms) - a muharib is a bandit or robber who terrorizes the public.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment in kind, especially for homicide or bodily harm.

Method of Crucifixion for the Muharib
Describes the prescribed method of crucifixion for the muharib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prescribed Hanafi method of crucifying the muharib and identify the key elements of the punishment.

Core Idea
The muharib is crucified alive and his belly pierced with a spear — the execution is part of the punishment, not post-mortem display.

The hadd punishment for muharib includes crucifixion (salb). The Hanafi school prescribes a specific method: the condemned is fastened to a cross while alive, then his abdomen is pierced with a spear until death. This lesson presents the exact ruling as recorded in the classical texts, emphasizing the active nature of the execution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being ruled upon
The act is the punishment of salb for the muharib. Recognize that this is a prescribed hadd punishment.
2
Recognize the sequence: alive, then pierced
The text explicitly states the order: 'yuslabu hayyan' (crucified alive) first, then 'yub'aju batnuhu' (belly pierced).
The piercing is not done after death.
3
Note the instrument: spear
The piercing is performed with a spear (rumh), specifying the tool used.
4
Determine the endpoint: until death
The piercing continues until the person dies ('ila an yamuta').
Death is the end point of the punishment.
5
Distinguish from other crucifixion methods
Unlike some practices, the Hanafi method requires the person to be alive during crucifixion, and death is caused by the piercing.
This distinguishes it from post-mortem display.

Source Text

[2565] (43) And he is crucified alive, and his belly is pierced with a spear until he dies.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is a ruling statement describing the method of crucifixion (salb) as punishment for the muharib. The condemned is to be fastened to a cross while alive, and then his abdomen is pierced with a spear causing death. The purpose is both execution and public deterrence.

Key Terms
صلب (salb): Crucifixion; fixing the body on a wooden plank or cross as a form of execution.
بعج (ba'aja): To pierce or rip open the abdomen.

Duration of Crucifixion: Three-Day Maximum
states the maximum period for leaving the crucified body

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum duration for leaving a muharib's body crucified and identify the legal ruling (hukm) for exceeding that period.

Core Idea
The crucified body must be taken down after three days.

This ruling specifies the time limit for crucifixion in Hanafi fiqh. The body should not be left on the cross beyond three days, after which it must be removed for burial. The wisdom behind this limit is to prevent decay and show respect, while still achieving the deterrent purpose.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Read the Arabic text and translation. The ruling is a prohibition: 'لا يصلب اكثر من ثلثة ايام' — he should not be crucified for more than three days.
The maximum is three days.
2
Identify the hukm
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'لا يفعل' indicates prohibition (tahrim). Therefore, leaving the body crucified beyond three days is haram.
The hukm is haram.
3
Understand the wisdom
The purpose of crucifixion is public deterrence. After three days, the body decays and causes harm, and the deterrence is already served.
Respect for the deceased.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf opined that the body may be left until the flesh falls off for greater deterrence, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the three-day limit.
Tarjih to three days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۵۶۶] (۴۴) ولا يصلب اكثر من ثلثة ايام
[2566] (44) And he should not be crucified for more than three days.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This is a ruling specifying the time limit for crucifixion. The body should not be left on the cross beyond three days. The reasoning given in the Urdu commentary is that after three days, the body decays and gives off foul odor; three days is sufficient for public deterrence. There is also a mention of Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion that it may be left until the flesh falls off for greater deterrence, but the text prefers the three-day limit.

Key Terms
صلب (salb): Crucifixion; fixing the body on a cross.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Three days
C) Seven days
D) Until the flesh falls off

Key Takeaway
The maximum period for crucifixion of a muharib is three days; exceeding that is haram.
